You're tapping into the concept of cybernetics, which is the study of systems, control, and communication in animals and machines. It's about how systems self-regulate through feedback loops.Here's a brief breakdown of some of the core concepts you touched upon:Sensation & Movement: You're drawing a parallel between sensing something and taking action, suggesting a deeply intertwined relationship. This is reminiscent of embodied cognition theories that posit the mind isn't just a product of the brain but also of the body's interactions with the environment.Activation Pathways: These seem to be mechanisms you use to modulate attention and action. By controlling the information you let in (aperture), you can better tune your reactions and sensory experiences.Attentional Pathways: This is a higher order of control, where you're governing the activation pathways. The left and right hemisphere distinctions you mention might be oversimplified (as both hemispheres collaborate extensively), but it's a useful tool for your introspection. The anecdote about "popsicle" hints at the interplay between hemispheres and how our cognition can influence perception and action.Cybernetic Definition of Life: The article you referenced relates to defining life through a cybernetic lens. The dual feedback mechanism - inferior negative feedbacks (keeping things in check) and a superior positive feedback (driving growth and expansion) - is a compelling way to distinguish living beings from inanimate objects. This mirrors your personal exploration of feedback systems in understanding behavior.Attentional Cladistics: You mention an "attentional cladistics," suggesting an evolutionary model of your attention patterns. Cladistics is a method in biology to classify organisms based on shared ancestry. By applying this concept to attention, you seem to be suggesting that your attention patterns have evolved over time and that you can trace back to foundational patterns that gave rise to more complex ones.In summary, your note is a blend of personal introspection and theoretical exploration, aiming to understand the self through the lens of cybernetics and feedback systems. It's a fascinating perspective that can provide valuable insights into cognition, behavior, and personal growth.YouDo you know the more recent paper, attention is all you need?ChatGPTChatGPTYes, "Attention Is All You Need" is a seminal paper from 2017 by Vaswani et al. that introduced the Transformer architecture, which has since revolutionized the field of natural language processing (NLP) and many other areas of machine learning.Here's a brief overview:Problem: Traditional sequence-to-sequence models used in tasks like machine translation often rely on RNNs (Recurrent Neural Networks) or LSTMs (Long Short-Term Memory networks). These architectures process sequences step-by-step, which makes them inherently sequential and harder to parallelize. This limits their efficiency on modern hardware.Solution: The Transformer model abandons the sequential nature of RNNs and instead processes input sequences entirely through self-attention mechanisms.Key Concepts:Self-Attention Mechanism: Allows the model to weigh the importance of different parts of the input data when producing an output. It helps the model focus on ("attend to") relevant parts of the input for a given task.Multi-Head Attention: Instead of having a single set of attention weights, the Transformer uses multiple sets, enabling it to focus on different parts of the input simultaneously.Positional Encoding: Since the model doesn't process data sequentially, it doesn't have a sense of order of the sequence. Positional encodings are added to give the model information about the position of words in a sequence.Impact:
The Transformer architecture led to a series of breakthrough models in NLP. BERT (Bidirectional Encoder Representations from Transformers), GPT (Generative Pretrained Transformer), and many other models are based on the Transformer architecture.The ChatGPT you're interacting with right now is a descendant of the Transformer model, based on the GPT architecture by OpenAI. The ideas presented in "Attention Is All You Need" have been foundational in advancing the capabilities of models like mine.YouConnections with my ideas for an Attentional CladisticsChatGPTChatGPTYour idea of "Attentional Cladistics" is unique in its approach and perspective, merging evolutionary principles with cognitive processes. Let's delve deeper into potential connections between your ideas and the Transformer's attention mechanism:Evolution of Attention Patterns:Attentional Cladistics: You proposed an evolutionary model for attention patterns, suggesting that foundational patterns give rise to more complex ones over time.Transformer: The self-attention mechanism allows the model to weigh the importance of different parts of the input data. Over training iterations, the model refines these weights, which can be seen as the evolution of attention patterns tailored to specific tasks.Parallel Processing:Attentional Cladistics: Your notes hint at the parallel nature of sensory experiences and processing multiple stimuli simultaneously.Transformer: It operates in parallel, processing entire sequences at once rather than sequentially. This mimics the brain's ability to process multiple sensory inputs concurrently.Feedback Loops:Attentional Cladistics: Your description emphasizes feedback systems, where sensory inputs and attention patterns interact and refine each other.Transformer: The multi-head attention allows the model to focus on different parts of the input simultaneously. This iterative refining process can be seen as a feedback loop, optimizing the model's attention over time.Hemispherical Distinctions:Attentional Cladistics: You mentioned switching focus between the left (for novel information) and right (for familiar information) hemispheres.Transformer: While it doesn't have an explicit left/right distinction, the multi-head attention can be likened to having multiple perspectives or approaches to a problem, analogous to how our brain uses different hemispheres for different tasks.Positional Understanding:Attentional Cladistics: Your focus on sensation and movement, and the relative positions of stimuli and how they're processed.Transformer: Positional encodings are vital for the Transformer to understand sequence order, similar to how our attention prioritizes certain stimuli based on their context or position.In essence, the Transformer's attention mechanism and your concept of "Attentional Cladistics" both center around the dynamic interplay of focus, context, and the adaptive processing of information. Your idea, grounded in evolutionary and cybernetic principles, provides a fascinating lens through which to understand and extend models like the Transformer.YouPsycholinguistics is sometimes def i ned as the study of language and 
the mind. As the name suggests, it is a subject which links psychology 
and linguistics. The common aim of all who call themselves psycholin- 
guists is to fi nd out about the structures and processes which underlie 
a humanâs ability to speak and understand language. 
Both psychologists and linguists are involved in studying psycholin- 
guistics. As one group of researchers has noted: 
The name says it all . . . it is simultaneously psychology and 
linguistics. At the heart of the discipline, therefore, is the relation- 
ship between these two fi elds, each of which can boast centuries 
of research tradition . . . By contrast, psycholinguistics itself is 
relatively young . . . psycholinguistics as we understand it today 
and as a discipline with its own name has only been in existence 
since the mid-twentieth century. (Cutler et al. 2005: 1) 
(A complete list of references quoted in the text is contained in the 
References on pp. 269â92.) 
Both psychologists and linguists can be classif i ed as social scientists, 
so in one way their approach has long been similar. All social scientists 
work by forming and testing hypotheses. For example, a psycholinguist 
might hypothesize that the speech of someone who is suffering from a 
progressive disease of the nervous system will disintegrate in a certain 
order, perhaps suggesting that the constructions the patient learned most 
recently will be the fi rst to disappear. This hypothesis will then be tested 
against data collected from the speech of someone who is brain-damaged. 
This is where psychologists and linguists sometimes differ. Psychologists 
test their hypotheses mainly by means of carefully controlled experiments. 
Linguists, on the other hand, test their hypotheses mainly by checking

It aims to uncover the underlying structures and processes that facilitate human language production and comprehension.Historical Context: The discipline of psycholinguistics, as understood today, is relatively young, having been formally named and recognized since the mid-20th century.Research Methods:Psychologists: They typically use controlled experiments to validate their hypotheses. 1animal communication; 
2child language; 
3the language of normal adults; 
4the speech of aphasics (people with speech disturbances). 
As the diagram below shows, these are not watertight compartments.

intrinsically linked together, and cannot easily be separated. It is far 
easier to split off phonology. Syntax and semantics together form the 
essence of any language. They, alongside the lexicon, will therefore 
be the basic concern of this book. Phonology will mostly be omitted, 
and only referred to where it illuminates syntactic and semantic 
problems. 
Perhaps here we need to mention also a vast and woolly subject 
which is not the concern of this book â the relationship of language 
to thought. Although it is clear that thought is possible without langu-

categories. This means that when we are discussing production and

when they communicate. They often manage to comprehend and

Let's dive deeper into the concept of "Attentional Cladistics" by trying to marry the ideas from your 2010 note with the principles of cladistics. I'll outline it as a hypothetical framework:

### 1. **Definition**: 
**Attentional Cladistics** could be understood as the study of the evolutionary lineage of cognitive attention patterns and strategies. It traces the divergence and evolution of attentional strategies in response to varying stimuli and environments.

### 2. **Basic Principles**:

- **Ancestral State**: Just as cladistics starts with a common ancestor, attentional cladistics would consider a foundational, primal attentional state from which all other attention patterns derive.

- **Derivative Patterns**: Over time, as new stimuli are encountered and new cognitive challenges faced, new attentional strategies would evolve and branch off from ancestral states.

### 3. **Features of Attention**:

- **Aperture**: The scope or breadth of attention. It determines how much information is allowed in at any given time.

- **Intensity**: The depth or sharpness of attention. It regulates how much information is sent out or acted upon.

- **Value System (Pleasure vs. Pain)**: The inherent value assigned to stimuli, which might drive attention.

### 4. **Mechanisms**:

- **Activation Pathways**: Represent the basic channels of attention, like sensory input sources.

- **Attentional Pathways**: Higher-order channels that modulate or govern the activation pathways.

### 5. **Evolutionary Adaptations**:

- **Hemispherical Shifts**: The idea of switching between different cognitive strategies (novel vs. familiar) based on hemispherical dominance.

- **Feedback Systems**: Adaptation based on the feedback received from an environment or internal state.

### 6. **Mapping Evolution**:

- **Attentional Trees**: Similar to phylogenetic trees in biology, one could trace the lineage of attention patterns, showing which strategies gave rise to others.

- **Derived Characters**: Key shifts or innovations in attentional strategy can be identified, akin to evolutionary adaptations in biological species.

### 7. **Applications**:

- **Personal Growth**: Understanding one's own attentional evolution can aid in personal development, helping to optimize attention in various situations.

- **Therapeutic Interventions**: Insights from attentional cladistics might inform therapeutic strategies, especially for attention-related disorders.

- **AI & Machine Learning**: By understanding the evolution of human attention, better models might be developed to mimic or complement human attention.

### 8. **Challenges**:

- **Quantification**: While biological cladistics can rely on genetic data, quantifying and objectively measuring attentional patterns would be challenging.

- **Subjectivity**: Attention is deeply personal, and there might be significant variation between individuals.

- **Environmental Interplay**: The environment plays a crucial role in shaping attention. Distinguishing between innate attentional patterns and those shaped purely by environment would be complex.

In essence, "Attentional Cladistics" offers a structured way to study the evolution of attention patterns, tracing their lineage, understanding their divergence, and applying this knowledge for personal and societal benefit. It bridges the gap between cognitive science, evolutionary biology, and personal introspection.ChatGPTChatGPTThis is a well-constructed outline!
